10150-8{_}629{_}turned up at the station at Frankfort, and casually remarked that he was going on to see the most all-fired old Methuselah of a town in Yurrup, and that he guessed that so much travelling alone was enough to send an intelligent, active citizen into the melancholy ward of a daft house, we took the pretty broad hint and suggested that we should join forces.
10150-8{_}630{_}We found, on comparing notes afterwards, that we had each intended to speak with some diffidence or hesitation so as not to appear too eager, such not being a good compliment to the success of our married life; but the effect was entirely marred by our both beginning to speak at the same instant--stopping simultaneously and then going on together again.
10150-8{_}631{_}Anyhow, no matter how, it was done; and Elias P. Hutcheson became one of our party.
10150-8{_}632{_}Straightway Amelia and I found the pleasant benefit; instead of quarrelling, as we had been doing, we found that the restraining influence of a third party was such that we now took every opportunity of spooning in odd corners.
10150-8{_}633{_}Amelia declares that ever since she has, as the result of that experience, advised all her friends to take a friend on the honeymoon.
10150-8{_}634{_}Well, we 'did' Nurnberg together, and much enjoyed the racy remarks of our Transatlantic friend, who, from his quaint speech and his wonderful stock of adventures, might have stepped out of a novel.
10150-8{_}635{_}We kept for the last object of interest in the city to be visited the Burg, and on the day appointed for the visit strolled round the outer wall of the city by the eastern side.
10150-8{_}636{_}The Burg is seated on a rock dominating the town and an immensely deep fosse guards it on the northern side.
10150-8{_}637{_}Nurnberg has been happy in that it was never sacked; had it been it would certainly not be so spick and span perfect as it is at present.
10150-8{_}638{_}The ditch has not been used for centuries, and now its base is spread with tea-gardens and orchards, of which some of the trees are of quite respectable growth.
10150-8{_}639{_}As we wandered round the wall, dawdling in the hot July sunshine, we often paused to admire the views spread before us, and in especial the great plain covered with towns and villages and bounded with a blue line of hills, like a landscape of Claude Lorraine.
10150-8{_}640{_}From this we always turned with new delight to the city itself, with its myriad of quaint old gables and acre-wide red roofs dotted with dormer windows, tier upon tier.
10150-8{_}641{_}A little to our right rose the towers of the Burg, and nearer still, standing grim, the Torture Tower, which was, and is, perhaps, the most interesting place in the city.
10150-8{_}642{_}For centuries the tradition of the Iron Virgin of Nurnberg has been handed down as an instance of the horrors of cruelty of which man is capable; we had long looked forward to seeing it; and here at last was its home.
10150-8{_}643{_}In one of our pauses we leaned over the wall of the moat and looked down.
10150-8{_}644{_}The garden seemed quite fifty or sixty feet below us, and the sun pouring into it with an intense, moveless heat like that of an oven.
10150-8{_}645{_}Beyond rose the grey, grim wall seemingly of endless height, and losing itself right and left in the angles of bastion and counterscarp.
10150-8{_}646{_}Trees and bushes crowned the wall, and above again towered the lofty houses on whose massive beauty Time has only set the hand of approval.
10150-8{_}647{_}The sun was hot and we were lazy; time was our own, and we lingered, leaning on the wall.
10150-8{_}648{_}Just below us was a pretty sight--a great black cat lying stretched in the sun, whilst round her gambolled prettily a tiny black kitten.
10150-8{_}649{_}The mother would wave her tail for the kitten to play with, or would raise her feet and push away the little one as an encouragement to further play.
10150-8{_}650{_}They were just at the foot of the wall, and Elias P. Hutcheson, in order to help the play, stooped and took from the walk a moderate sized pebble.
10150-8{_}651{_}'See!'
10150-8{_}652{_}he said, 'I will drop it near the kitten, and they will both wonder where it came from.'
10150-8{_}653{_}'Oh, be careful,' said my wife; 'you might hit the dear little thing!'
10150-8{_}654{_}'Not me, ma'am,' said Elias P. 'Why, I'm as tender as a Maine cherry-tree.
10150-8{_}655{_}Lor, bless ye.
10150-8{_}656{_}I wouldn't hurt the poor pooty little critter more'n I'd scalp a baby.
10150-8{_}657{_}An' you may bet your variegated socks on that!
10150-8{_}658{_}See, I'll drop it fur away on the outside so's not to go near her!'
10150-8{_}659{_}Thus saying, he leaned over and held his arm out at full length and dropped the stone.
10150-8{_}660{_}It may be that there is some attractive force which draws lesser matters to greater; or more probably that the wall was not plump but sloped to its base--we not noticing the inclination from above; but the stone fell with a sickening thud that came up to us through the hot air, right on the kitten's head, and shattered out its little brains then and there.
10150-8{_}661{_}The black cat cast a swift upward glance, and we saw her eyes like green fire fixed an instant on Elias P. Hutcheson; and then her attention was given to the kitten, which lay still with just a quiver of her tiny limbs, whilst a thin red stream trickled from a gaping wound.
10150-8{_}662{_}With a muffled cry, such as a human being might give, she bent over the kitten licking its wounds and moaning.
10150-8{_}663{_}Suddenly she seemed to realise that it was dead, and again threw her eyes up at us.
10150-8{_}664{_}I shall never forget the sight, for she looked the perfect incarnation of hate.
10150-8{_}665{_}Her green eyes blazed with lurid fire, and the white, sharp teeth seemed to almost shine through the blood which dabbled her mouth and whiskers.
10150-8{_}666{_}She gnashed her teeth, and her claws stood out stark and at full length on every paw.
10150-8{_}667{_}Then she made a wild rush up the wall as if to reach us, but when the momentum ended fell back, and further added to her horrible appearance for she fell on the kitten, and rose with her black fur smeared with its brains and blood.
10150-8{_}668{_}Amelia turned quite faint, and I had to lift her back from the wall.
10150-8{_}669{_}There was a seat close by in shade of a spreading plane-tree, and here I placed her whilst she composed herself.
10150-8{_}670{_}Then I went back to Hutcheson, who stood without moving, looking down on the angry cat below.
10150-8{_}671{_}As I joined him, he said:  'Wall, I guess that air the savagest beast I ever see--'cept once when an Apache squaw had an edge on a half-breed what they nicknamed "Splinters" 'cos of the way he fixed up her papoose which he stole on a raid just to show that he appreciated the way they had given his mother the fire torture.
10150-8{_}672{_}She got that kinder look so set on her face that it jest seemed to grow there.
10150-8{_}673{_}She followed Splinters mor'n three year till at last the braves got him and handed him over to her.
10150-8{_}674{_}They did say that no man, white or Injun, had ever been so long a-dying under the tortures of the Apaches.
10150-8{_}675{_}The only time I ever see her smile was when I wiped her out.
10150-8{_}676{_}I kem on the camp just in time to see Splinters pass in his checks, and he wasn't sorry to go either.
10150-8{_}677{_}He was a hard citizen, and though I never could shake with him after that papoose business--for it was bitter bad, and he should have been a white man, for he looked like one--I see he had got paid out in full.
10150-8{_}678{_}Durn me, but I took a piece of his hide from one of his skinnin' posts an' had it made into a pocket-book.
10150-8{_}679{_}It's here now!'
10150-8{_}680{_}and he slapped the breast pocket of his coat.
10150-8{_}681{_}Whilst he was speaking the cat was continuing her frantic efforts to get up the wall.
10150-8{_}682{_}She would take a run back and then charge up, sometimes reaching an incredible height.
10150-8{_}683{_}She did not seem to mind the heavy fall which she got each time but started with renewed vigour; and at every tumble her appearance became more horrible.
10150-8{_}684{_}Hutcheson was a kind-hearted man--my wife and I had both noticed little acts of kindness to animals as well as to persons--and he seemed concerned at the state of fury to which the cat had wrought herself.
10150-8{_}685{_}'Wall, now!'
10150-8{_}686{_}he said, 'I du declare that that poor critter seems quite desperate.
10150-8{_}687{_}There!
10150-8{_}688{_}there!
10150-8{_}689{_}poor thing, it was all an accident--though that won't bring back your little one to you.
10150-8{_}690{_}Say!
10150-8{_}691{_}I wouldn't have had such a thing happen for a thousand!
10150-8{_}692{_}Just shows what a clumsy fool of a man can do when he tries to play!
10150-8{_}693{_}Seems I'm too darned slipperhanded to even play with a cat.
10150-8{_}694{_}Say Colonel!'
10150-8{_}695{_}it was a pleasant way he had to bestow titles freely--'I hope your wife don't hold no grudge against me on account of this unpleasantness?
10150-8{_}696{_}Why, I wouldn't have had it occur on no account.'
10150-8{_}697{_}He came over to Amelia and apologised profusely, and she with her usual kindness of heart hastened to assure him that she quite understood that it was an accident.
10150-8{_}698{_}Then we all went again to the wall and looked over.
10150-8{_}699{_}The cat missing Hutcheson's face had drawn back across the moat, and was sitting on her haunches as though ready to spring.
10150-8{_}700{_}Indeed, the very instant she saw him she did spring, and with a blind unreasoning fury, which would have been grotesque, only that it was so frightfully real.
10150-8{_}701{_}She did not try to run up the wall, but simply launched herself at him as though hate and fury could lend her wings to pass straight through the great distance between them.
10150-8{_}702{_}Amelia, womanlike, got quite concerned, and said to Elias P. in a warning voice:  'Oh!
10150-8{_}703{_}you must be very careful.
10150-8{_}704{_}That animal would try to kill you if she were here; her eyes look like positive murder.'
10150-8{_}705{_}He laughed out jovially.
10150-8{_}706{_}'Excuse me, ma'am,' he said, 'but I can't help laughin'.
10150-8{_}707{_}Fancy a man that has fought grizzlies an' Injuns bein' careful of bein' murdered by a cat!'
10150-8{_}708{_}When the cat heard him laugh, her whole demeanour seemed to change.
10150-8{_}709{_}She no longer tried to jump or run up the wall, but went quietly over, and sitting again beside the dead kitten began to lick and fondle it as though it were alive.
10150-8{_}710{_}'See!'
10150-8{_}711{_}said I, 'the effect of a really strong man.
10150-8{_}712{_}Even that animal in the midst of her fury recognises the voice of a master, and bows to him!'
10150-8{_}713{_}'Like a squaw!'
10150-8{_}714{_}was the only comment of Elias P. Hutcheson, as we moved on our way round the city fosse.
10150-8{_}715{_}Every now and then we looked over the wall and each time saw the cat following us.
10150-8{_}716{_}At first she had kept going back to the dead kitten, and then as the distance grew greater took it in her mouth and so followed.
10150-8{_}717{_}After a while, however, she abandoned this, for we saw her following all alone; she had evidently hidden the body somewhere.
10150-8{_}718{_}Amelia's alarm grew at the cat's persistence, and more than once she repeated her warning; but the American always laughed with amusement, till finally, seeing that she was beginning to be worried, he said:  'I say, ma'am, you needn't be skeered over that cat.
10150-8{_}719{_}I go heeled, I du!'
10150-8{_}720{_}Here he slapped his pistol pocket at the back of his lumbar region.
10150-8{_}721{_}'Why sooner'n have you worried, I'll shoot the critter, right here, an' risk the police interferin' with a citizen of the United States for carryin' arms contrairy to reg'lations!'
10150-8{_}722{_}As he spoke he looked over the wall, but the cat on seeing him, retreated, with a growl, into a bed of tall flowers, and was hidden.
10150-8{_}723{_}He went on: 'Blest if that ar critter ain't got more sense of what's good for her than most Christians.
10150-8{_}724{_}I guess we've seen the last of her!
10150-8{_}725{_}You bet, she'll go back now to that busted kitten and have a private funeral of it, all to herself!'
10150-8{_}726{_}Amelia did not like to say more, lest he might, in mistaken kindness to her, fulfil his threat of shooting the cat: and so we went on and crossed the little wooden bridge leading to the gateway whence ran the steep paved roadway between the Burg and the pentagonal Torture Tower.
10150-8{_}727{_}As we crossed the bridge we saw the cat again down below us.
10150-8{_}728{_}When she saw us her fury seemed to return, and she made frantic efforts to get up the steep wall.
10150-8{_}729{_}Hutcheson laughed as he looked down at her, and said:  'Goodbye, old girl.
10150-8{_}730{_}Sorry I injured your feelin's, but you'll get over it in time!
10150-8{_}731{_}So long!'
10150-8{_}732{_}And then we passed through the long, dim archway and came to the gate of the Burg.
10150-8{_}733{_}When we came out again after our survey of this most beautiful old place which not even the well-intentioned efforts of the Gothic restorers of forty years ago have been able to spoil--though their restoration was then glaring white--we seemed to have quite forgotten the unpleasant episode of the morning.
10150-8{_}734{_}The old lime tree with its great trunk gnarled with the passing of nearly nine centuries, the deep well cut through the heart of the rock by those captives of old, and the lovely view from the city wall whence we heard, spread over almost a full quarter of an hour, the multitudinous chimes of the city, had all helped to wipe out from our minds the incident of the slain kitten.
10150-8{_}735{_}We were the only visitors who had entered the Torture Tower that morning--so at least said the old custodian--and as we had the place all to ourselves were able to make a minute and more satisfactory survey than would have otherwise been possible.
10150-8{_}736{_}The custodian, looking to us as the sole source of his gains for the day, was willing to meet our wishes in any way.
10150-8{_}737{_}The Torture Tower is truly a grim place, even now when many thousands of visitors have sent a stream of life, and the joy that follows life, into the place; but at the time I mention it wore its grimmest and most gruesome aspect.
10150-8{_}738{_}The dust of ages seemed to have settled on it, and the darkness and the horror of its memories seem to have become sentient in a way that would have satisfied the Pantheistic souls of Philo or Spinoza.
10150-8{_}739{_}The lower chamber where we entered was seemingly, in its normal state, filled with incarnate darkness; even the hot sunlight streaming in through the door seemed to be lost in the vast thickness of the walls, and only showed the masonry rough as when the builder's scaffolding had come down, but coated with dust and marked here and there with patches of dark stain which, if walls could speak, could have given their own dread memories of fear and pain.
10150-8{_}740{_}We were glad to pass up the dusty wooden staircase, the custodian leaving the outer door open to light us somewhat on our way; for to our eyes the one long-wick'd, evil-smelling candle stuck in a sconce on the wall gave an inadequate light.
10150-8{_}741{_}When we came up through the open trap in the corner of the chamber overhead, Amelia held on to me so tightly that I could actually feel her heart beat.
10150-8{_}742{_}I must say for my own part that I was not surprised at her fear, for this room was even more gruesome than that below.
10150-8{_}743{_}Here there was certainly more light, but only just sufficient to realise the horrible surroundings of the place.
10150-8{_}744{_}The builders of the tower had evidently intended that only they who should gain the top should have any of the joys of light and prospect.
10150-8{_}745{_}There, as we had noticed from below, were ranges of windows, albeit of mediaeval smallness, but elsewhere in the tower were only a very few narrow slits such as were habitual in places of mediaeval defence.
10150-8{_}746{_}A few of these only lit the chamber, and these so high up in the wall that from no part could the sky be seen through the thickness of the walls.
10150-8{_}747{_}In racks, and leaning in disorder against the walls, were a number of headsmen's swords, great double-handed weapons with broad blade and keen edge.
10150-8{_}748{_}Hard by were several blocks whereon the necks of the victims had lain, with here and there deep notches where the steel had bitten through the guard of flesh and shored into the wood.
10150-8{_}749{_}Round the chamber, placed in all sorts of irregular ways, were many implements of torture which made one's heart ache to see--chairs full of spikes which gave instant and excruciating pain; chairs and couches with dull knobs whose torture was seemingly less, but which, though slower, were equally efficacious; racks, belts, boots, gloves, collars, all made for compressing at will; steel baskets in which the head could be slowly crushed into a pulp if necessary; watchmen's hooks with long handle and knife that cut at resistance--this a speciality of the old Nurnberg police system; and many, many other devices for man's injury to man.
10150-8{_}750{_}Amelia grew quite pale with the horror of the things, but fortunately did not faint, for being a little overcome she sat down on a torture chair, but jumped up again with a shriek, all tendency to faint gone.
10150-8{_}751{_}We both pretended that it was the injury done to her dress by the dust of the chair, and the rusty spikes which had upset her, and Mr. Hutcheson acquiesced in accepting the explanation with a kind-hearted laugh.
10150-8{_}752{_}But the central object in the whole of this chamber of horrors was the engine known as the Iron Virgin, which stood near the centre of the room.
10150-8{_}753{_}It was a rudely-shaped figure of a woman, something of the bell order, or, to make a closer comparison, of the figure of Mrs. Noah in the children's Ark, but without that slimness of waist and perfect _rondeur_ of hip which marks the aesthetic type of the Noah family.
10150-8{_}754{_}One would hardly have recognised it as intended for a human figure at all had not the founder shaped on the forehead a rude semblance of a woman's face.
10150-8{_}755{_}This machine was coated with rust without, and covered with dust; a rope was fastened to a ring in the front of the figure, about where the waist should have been, and was drawn through a pulley, fastened on the wooden pillar which sustained the flooring above.
10150-8{_}756{_}The custodian pulling this rope showed that a section of the front was hinged like a door at one side; we then saw that the engine was of considerable thickness, leaving just room enough inside for a man to be placed.
10150-8{_}757{_}The door was of equal thickness and of great weight, for it took the custodian all his strength, aided though he was by the contrivance of the pulley, to open it.
10150-8{_}758{_}This weight was partly due to the fact that the door was of manifest purpose hung so as to throw its weight downwards, so that it might shut of its own accord when the strain was released.
10150-8{_}759{_}The inside was honeycombed with rust--nay more, the rust alone that comes through time would hardly have eaten so deep into the iron walls; the rust of the cruel stains was deep indeed!
10150-8{_}760{_}It was only, however, when we came to look at the inside of the door that the diabolical intention was manifest to the full.
10150-8{_}761{_}Here were several long spikes, square and massive, broad at the base and sharp at the points, placed in such a position that when the door should close the upper ones would pierce the eyes of the victim, and the lower ones his heart and vitals.
10150-8{_}762{_}The sight was too much for poor Amelia, and this time she fainted dead off, and I had to carry her down the stairs, and place her on a bench outside till she recovered.
10150-8{_}763{_}That she felt it to the quick was afterwards shown by the fact that my eldest son bears to this day a rude birthmark on his breast, which has, by family consent, been accepted as representing the Nurnberg Virgin.
10150-8{_}764{_}When we got back to the chamber we found Hutcheson still opposite the Iron Virgin; he had been evidently philosophising, and now gave us the benefit of his thought in the shape of a sort of exordium.
10150-8{_}765{_}'Wall, I guess I've been learnin' somethin' here while madam has been gettin' over her faint.
10150-8{_}766{_}'Pears to me that we're a long way behind the times on our side of the big drink.
10150-8{_}767{_}We uster think out on the plains that the Injun could give us points in tryin' to make a man uncomfortable; but I guess your old mediaeval law-and-order party could raise him every time.
10150-8{_}768{_}Splinters was pretty good in his bluff on the squaw, but this here young miss held a straight flush all high on him.
10150-8{_}769{_}The points of them spikes air sharp enough still, though even the edges air eaten out by what uster be on them.
10150-8{_}770{_}It'd be a good thing for our Indian section to get some specimens of this here play-toy to send round to the Reservations jest to knock the stuffin' out of the bucks, and the squaws too, by showing them as how old civilisation lays over them at their best.
10150-8{_}771{_}Guess but I'll get in that box a minute jest to see how it feels!'
10150-8{_}772{_}'Oh no!
10150-8{_}773{_}no!'
10150-8{_}774{_}said Amelia.
10150-8{_}775{_}'It is too terrible!'
10150-8{_}776{_}'Guess, ma'am, nothin's too terrible to the explorin' mind.
10150-8{_}777{_}I've been in some queer places in my time.
10150-8{_}778{_}Spent a night inside a dead horse while a prairie fire swept over me in Montana Territory--an' another time slept inside a dead buffler when the Comanches was on the war path an' I didn't keer to leave my kyard on them.
10150-8{_}779{_}I've been two days in a caved-in tunnel in the Billy Broncho gold mine in New Mexico, an' was one of the four shut up for three parts of a day in the caisson what slid over on her side when we was settin' the foundations of the Buffalo Bridge.
10150-8{_}780{_}I've not funked an odd experience yet, an' I don't propose to begin now!'
10150-8{_}781{_}We saw that he was set on the experiment, so I said: 'Well, hurry up, old man, and get through it quick!'
10150-8{_}782{_}'All right, General,' said he, 'but I calculate we ain't quite ready yet.
10150-8{_}783{_}The gentlemen, my predecessors, what stood in that thar canister, didn't volunteer for the office--not much!
10150-8{_}784{_}And I guess there was some ornamental tyin' up before the big stroke was made.
10150-8{_}785{_}I want to go into this thing fair and square, so I must get fixed up proper first.
10150-8{_}786{_}I dare say this old galoot can rise some string and tie me up accordin' to sample?'
10150-8{_}787{_}This was said interrogatively to the old custodian, but the latter, who understood the drift of his speech, though perhaps not appreciating to the full the niceties of dialect and imagery, shook his head.
10150-8{_}788{_}His protest was, however, only formal and made to be overcome.
10150-8{_}789{_}The American thrust a gold piece into his hand, saying: 'Take it, pard!
10150-8{_}790{_}it's your pot; and don't be skeer'd.
10150-8{_}791{_}This ain't no necktie party that you're asked to assist in!'
10150-8{_}792{_}He produced some thin frayed rope and proceeded to bind our companion with sufficient strictness for the purpose.
10150-8{_}793{_}When the upper part of his body was bound, Hutcheson said:  'Hold on a moment, Judge.
10150-8{_}794{_}Guess I'm too heavy for you to tote into the canister.
10150-8{_}795{_}You jest let me walk in, and then you can wash up regardin' my legs!'
10150-8{_}796{_}Whilst speaking he had backed himself into the opening which was just enough to hold him.
10150-8{_}797{_}It was a close fit and no mistake.
10150-8{_}798{_}Amelia looked on with fear in her eyes, but she evidently did not like to say anything.
10150-8{_}799{_}Then the custodian completed his task by tying the American's feet together so that he was now absolutely helpless and fixed in his voluntary prison.
10150-8{_}800{_}He seemed to really enjoy it, and the incipient smile which was habitual to his face blossomed into actuality as he said:  'Guess this here Eve was made out of the rib of a dwarf!
10150-8{_}801{_}There ain't much room for a full-grown citizen of the United States to hustle.
10150-8{_}802{_}We uster make our coffins more roomier in Idaho territory.
10150-8{_}803{_}Now, Judge, you jest begin to let this door down, slow, on to me.
10150-8{_}804{_}I want to feel the same pleasure as the other jays had when those spikes began to move toward their eyes!'
10150-8{_}805{_}'Oh no!
10150-8{_}806{_}no!
10150-8{_}807{_}no!'
10150-8{_}808{_}broke in Amelia hysterically.
10150-8{_}809{_}'It is too terrible!
10150-8{_}810{_}I can't bear to see it!--I can't!
10150-8{_}811{_}I can't!'
10150-8{_}812{_}But the American was obdurate.
10150-8{_}813{_}'Say, Colonel,' said he, 'why not take Madame for a little promenade?
10150-8{_}814{_}I wouldn't hurt her feelin's for the world; but now that I am here, havin' kem eight thousand miles, wouldn't it be too hard to give up the very experience I've been pinin' an' pantin' fur?
10150-8{_}815{_}A man can't get to feel like canned goods every time!
10150-8{_}816{_}Me and the Judge here'll fix up this thing in no time, an' then you'll come back, an' we'll all laugh together!'
10150-8{_}817{_}Once more the resolution that is born of curiosity triumphed, and Amelia stayed holding tight to my arm and shivering whilst the custodian began to slacken slowly inch by inch the rope that held back the iron door.
10150-8{_}818{_}Hutcheson's face was positively radiant as his eyes followed the first movement of the spikes.
10150-8{_}819{_}'Wall!'
10150-8{_}820{_}he said, 'I guess I've not had enjoyment like this since I left Noo York.
10150-8{_}821{_}Bar a scrap with a French sailor at Wapping--an' that warn't much of a picnic neither--I've not had a show fur real pleasure in this dod-rotted Continent, where there ain't no b'ars nor no Injuns, an' wheer nary man goes heeled.
10150-8{_}822{_}Slow there, Judge!
10150-8{_}823{_}Don't you rush this business!
10150-8{_}824{_}I want a show for my money this game--I du!'
10150-8{_}825{_}The custodian must have had in him some of the blood of his predecessors in that ghastly tower, for he worked the engine with a deliberate and excruciating slowness which after five minutes, in which the outer edge of the door had not moved half as many inches, began to overcome Amelia.
10150-8{_}826{_}I saw her lips whiten, and felt her hold upon my arm relax.
10150-8{_}827{_}I looked around an instant for a place whereon to lay her, and when I looked at her again found that her eye had become fixed on the side of the Virgin.
10150-8{_}828{_}Following its direction I saw the black cat crouching out of sight.
10150-8{_}829{_}Her green eyes shone like danger lamps in the gloom of the place, and their colour was heightened by the blood which still smeared her coat and reddened her mouth.
10150-8{_}830{_}I cried out:  'The cat!
10150-8{_}831{_}look out for the cat!'
10150-8{_}832{_}for even then she sprang out before the engine.
10150-8{_}833{_}At this moment she looked like a triumphant demon.
10150-8{_}834{_}Her eyes blazed with ferocity, her hair bristled out till she seemed twice her normal size, and her tail lashed about as does a tiger's when the quarry is before it.
10150-8{_}835{_}Elias P. Hutcheson when he saw her was amused, and his eyes positively sparkled with fun as he said:  'Darned if the squaw hain't got on all her war paint!
10150-8{_}836{_}Jest give her a shove off if she comes any of her tricks on me, for I'm so fixed everlastingly by the boss, that durn my skin if I can keep my eyes from her if she wants them!
10150-8{_}837{_}Easy there, Judge!
10150-8{_}838{_}don't you slack that ar rope or I'm euchered!'
10150-8{_}839{_}At this moment Amelia completed her faint, and I had to clutch hold of her round the waist or she would have fallen to the floor.
10150-8{_}840{_}Whilst attending to her I saw the black cat crouching for a spring, and jumped up to turn the creature out.
10150-8{_}841{_}But at that instant, with a sort of hellish scream, she hurled herself, not as we expected at Hutcheson, but straight at the face of the custodian.
10150-8{_}842{_}Her claws seemed to be tearing wildly as one sees in the Chinese drawings of the dragon rampant, and as I looked I saw one of them light on the poor man's eye, and actually tear through it and down his cheek, leaving a wide band of red where the blood seemed to spurt from every vein.
10150-8{_}843{_}With a yell of sheer terror which came quicker than even his sense of pain, the man leaped back, dropping as he did so the rope which held back the iron door.
10150-8{_}844{_}I jumped for it, but was too late, for the cord ran like lightning through the pulley-block, and the heavy mass fell forward from its own weight.
10150-8{_}845{_}As the door closed I caught a glimpse of our poor companion's face.
10150-8{_}846{_}He seemed frozen with terror.
10150-8{_}847{_}His eyes stared with a horrible anguish as if dazed, and no sound came from his lips.
10150-8{_}848{_}And then the spikes did their work.
10150-8{_}849{_}Happily the end was quick, for when I wrenched open the door they had pierced so deep that they had locked in the bones of the skull through which they had crushed, and actually tore him--it--out of his iron prison till, bound as he was, he fell at full length with a sickly thud upon the floor, the face turning upward as he fell.
10150-8{_}850{_}I rushed to my wife, lifted her up and carried her out, for I feared for her very reason if she should wake from her faint to such a scene.
10150-8{_}851{_}I laid her on the bench outside and ran back.
10150-8{_}852{_}Leaning against the wooden column was the custodian moaning in pain whilst he held his reddening handkerchief to his eyes.
10150-8{_}853{_}And sitting on the head of the poor American was the cat, purring loudly as she licked the blood which trickled through the gashed socket of his eyes.
10150-8{_}854{_}I think no one will call me cruel because I seized one of the old executioner's swords and shore her in two as she sat.
10150-8{_}855{_}The Secret of the Growing Gold   When Margaret Delandre went to live at Brent's Rock the whole neighbourhood awoke to the pleasure of an entirely new scandal.
10150-8{_}856{_}Scandals in connection with either the Delandre family or the Brents of Brent's Rock, were not few; and if the secret history of the county had been written in full both names would have been found well represented.
10150-8{_}857{_}It is true that the status of each was so different that they might have belonged to different continents--or to different worlds for the matter of that--for hitherto their orbits had never crossed.
10150-8{_}858{_}The Brents were accorded by the whole section of the country a unique social dominance, and had ever held themselves as high above the yeoman class to which Margaret Delandre belonged, as a blue-blooded Spanish hidalgo out-tops his peasant tenantry.
10150-8{_}859{_}The Delandres had an ancient record and were proud of it in their way as the Brents were of theirs.
10150-8{_}860{_}But the family had never risen above yeomanry; and although they had been once well-to-do in the good old times of foreign wars and protection, their fortunes had withered under the scorching of the free trade sun and the 'piping times of peace.'
10150-8{_}861{_}They had, as the elder members used to assert, 'stuck to the land', with the result that they had taken root in it, body and soul.
10150-8{_}862{_}In fact, they, having chosen the life of vegetables, had flourished as vegetation does--blossomed and thrived in the good season and suffered in the bad.
10150-8{_}863{_}Their holding, Dander's Croft, seemed to have been worked out, and to be typical of the family which had inhabited it.
10150-8{_}864{_}The latter had declined generation after generation, sending out now and again some abortive shoot of unsatisfied energy in the shape of a soldier or sailor, who had worked his way to the minor grades of the services and had there stopped, cut short either from unheeding gallantry in action or from that destroying cause to men without breeding or youthful care--the recognition of a position above them which they feel unfitted to fill.
10150-8{_}865{_}So, little by little, the family dropped lower and lower, the men brooding and dissatisfied, and drinking themselves into the grave, the women drudging at home, or marrying beneath them--or worse.
10150-8{_}866{_}In process of time all disappeared, leaving only two in the Croft, Wykham Delandre and his sister Margaret.
10150-8{_}867{_}The man and woman seemed to have inherited in masculine and feminine form respectively the evil tendency of their race, sharing in common the principles, though manifesting them in different ways, of sullen passion, voluptuousness and recklessness.
10150-8{_}868{_}The history of the Brents had been something similar, but showing the causes of decadence in their aristocratic and not their plebeian forms.
10150-8{_}869{_}They, too, had sent their shoots to the wars; but their positions had been different and they had often attained honour--for without flaw they were gallant, and brave deeds were done by them before the selfish dissipation which marked them had sapped their vigour.
10150-8{_}870{_}The present head of the family--if family it could now be called when one remained of the direct line--was Geoffrey Brent.
10150-8{_}871{_}He was almost a type of worn out race, manifesting in some ways its most brilliant qualities, and in others its utter degradation.
10150-8{_}872{_}He might be fairly compared with some of those antique Italian nobles whom the painters have preserved to us with their courage, their unscrupulousness, their refinement of lust and cruelty--the voluptuary actual with the fiend potential.
10150-8{_}873{_}He was certainly handsome, with that dark, aquiline, commanding beauty which women so generally recognise as dominant.
10150-8{_}874{_}With men he was distant and cold; but such a bearing never deters womankind.
10150-8{_}875{_}The inscrutable laws of sex have so arranged that even a timid woman is not afraid of a fierce and haughty man.
10150-8{_}876{_}And so it was that there was hardly a woman of any kind or degree, who lived within view of Brent's Rock, who did not cherish some form of secret admiration for the handsome wastrel.
10150-8{_}877{_}The category was a wide one, for Brent's Rock rose up steeply from the midst of a level region and for a circuit of a hundred miles it lay on the horizon, with its high old towers and steep roofs cutting the level edge of wood and hamlet, and far-scattered mansions.
10150-8{_}878{_}So long as Geoffrey Brent confined his dissipations to London and Paris and Vienna--anywhere out of sight and sound of his home--opinion was silent.
10150-8{_}879{_}It is easy to listen to far off echoes unmoved, and we can treat them with disbelief, or scorn, or disdain, or whatever attitude of coldness may suit our purpose.
10150-8{_}880{_}But when the scandal came close home it was another matter; and the feelings of independence and integrity which is in people of every community which is not utterly spoiled, asserted itself and demanded that condemnation should be expressed.
10150-8{_}881{_}Still there was a certain reticence in all, and no more notice was taken of the existing facts than was absolutely necessary.
10150-8{_}882{_}Margaret Delandre bore herself so fearlessly and so openly--she accepted her position as the justified companion of Geoffrey Brent so naturally that people came to believe that she was secretly married to him, and therefore thought it wiser to hold their tongues lest time should justify her and also make her an active enemy.
10150-8{_}883{_}The one person who, by his interference, could have settled all doubts was debarred by circumstances from interfering in the matter.
10150-8{_}884{_}Wykham Delandre had quarrelled with his sister--or perhaps it was that she had quarrelled with him--and they were on terms not merely of armed neutrality but of bitter hatred.
10150-8{_}885{_}The quarrel had been antecedent to Margaret going to Brent's Rock.
10150-8{_}886{_}She and Wykham had almost come to blows.
10150-8{_}887{_}There had certainly been threats on one side and on the other; and in the end Wykham, overcome with passion, had ordered his sister to leave his house.
10150-8{_}888{_}She had risen straightway, and, without waiting to pack up even her own personal belongings, had walked out of the house.
10150-8{_}889{_}On the threshold she had paused for a moment to hurl a bitter threat at Wykham that he would rue in shame and despair to the last hour of his life his act of that day.
10150-8{_}890{_}Some weeks had since passed; and it was understood in the neighbourhood that Margaret had gone to London, when she suddenly appeared driving out with Geoffrey Brent, and the entire neighbourhood knew before nightfall that she had taken up her abode at the Rock.
10150-8{_}891{_}It was no subject of surprise that Brent had come back unexpectedly, for such was his usual custom.
10150-8{_}892{_}Even his own servants never knew when to expect him, for there was a private door, of which he alone had the key, by which he sometimes entered without anyone in the house being aware of his coming.
10150-8{_}893{_}This was his usual method of appearing after a long absence.
10150-8{_}894{_}Wykham Delandre was furious at the news.
10150-8{_}895{_}He vowed vengeance--and to keep his mind level with his passion drank deeper than ever.
10150-8{_}896{_}He tried several times to see his sister, but she contemptuously refused to meet him.
10150-8{_}897{_}He tried to have an interview with Brent and was refused by him also.
10150-8{_}898{_}Then he tried to stop him in the road, but without avail, for Geoffrey was not a man to be stopped against his will.
10150-8{_}899{_}Several actual encounters took place between the two men, and many more were threatened and avoided.
10150-8{_}900{_}At last Wykham Delandre settled down to a morose, vengeful acceptance of the situation.
10150-8{_}901{_}Neither Margaret nor Geoffrey was of a pacific temperament, and it was not long before there began to be quarrels between them.
10150-8{_}902{_}One thing would lead to another, and wine flowed freely at Brent's Rock.
10150-8{_}903{_}Now and again the quarrels would assume a bitter aspect, and threats would be exchanged in uncompromising language that fairly awed the listening servants.
10150-8{_}904{_}But such quarrels generally ended where domestic altercations do, in reconciliation, and in a mutual respect for the fighting qualities proportionate to their manifestation.
10150-8{_}905{_}Fighting for its own sake is found by a certain class of persons, all the world over, to be a matter of absorbing interest, and there is no reason to believe that domestic conditions minimise its potency.
10150-8{_}906{_}Geoffrey and Margaret made occasional absences from Brent's Rock, and on each of these occasions Wykham Delandre also absented himself; but as he generally heard of the absence too late to be of any service, he returned home each time in a more bitter and discontented frame of mind than before.
10150-8{_}907{_}At last there came a time when the absence from Brent's Rock became longer than before.
10150-8{_}908{_}Only a few days earlier there had been a quarrel, exceeding in bitterness anything which had gone before; but this, too, had been made up, and a trip on the Continent had been mentioned before the servants.
10150-8{_}909{_}After a few days Wykham Delandre also went away, and it was some weeks before he returned.
10150-8{_}910{_}It was noticed that he was full of some new importance--satisfaction, exaltation--they hardly knew how to call it.
10150-8{_}911{_}He went straightway to Brent's Rock, and demanded to see Geoffrey Brent, and on being told that he had not yet returned, said, with a grim decision which the servants noted:  'I shall come again.
10150-8{_}912{_}My news is solid--it can wait!'
10150-8{_}913{_}and turned away.
10150-8{_}914{_}Week after week went by, and month after month; and then there came a rumour, certified later on, that an accident had occurred in the Zermatt valley.
10150-8{_}915{_}Whilst crossing a dangerous pass the carriage containing an English lady and the driver had fallen over a precipice, the gentleman of the party, Mr. Geoffrey Brent, having been fortunately saved as he had been walking up the hill to ease the horses.
10150-8{_}916{_}He gave information, and search was made.
10150-8{_}917{_}The broken rail, the excoriated roadway, the marks where the horses had struggled on the decline before finally pitching over into the torrent--all told the sad tale.
10150-8{_}918{_}It was a wet season, and there had been much snow in the winter, so that the river was swollen beyond its usual volume, and the eddies of the stream were packed with ice.
10150-8{_}919{_}All search was made, and finally the wreck of the carriage and the body of one horse were found in an eddy of the river.
10150-8{_}920{_}Later on the body of the driver was found on the sandy, torrent-swept waste near Täsch; but the body of the lady, like that of the other horse, had quite disappeared, and was--what was left of it by that time--whirling amongst the eddies of the Rhone on its way down to the Lake of Geneva.
10150-8{_}921{_}Wykham Delandre made all the enquiries possible, but could not find any trace of the missing woman.
10150-8{_}922{_}He found, however, in the books of the various hotels the name of 'Mr.
10150-8{_}923{_}and Mrs. Geoffrey Brent'.
10150-8{_}924{_}And he had a stone erected at Zermatt to his sister's memory, under her married name, and a tablet put up in the church at Bretten, the parish in which both Brent's Rock and Dander's Croft were situated.
10150-8{_}925{_}There was a lapse of nearly a year, after the excitement of the matter had worn away, and the whole neighbourhood had gone on its accustomed way.
10150-8{_}926{_}Brent was still absent, and Delandre more drunken, more morose, and more revengeful than before.
10150-8{_}927{_}Then there was a new excitement.
10150-8{_}928{_}Brent's Rock was being made ready for a new mistress.
10150-8{_}929{_}It was officially announced by Geoffrey himself in a letter to the Vicar, that he had been married some months before to an Italian lady, and that they were then on their way home.
10150-8{_}930{_}Then a small army of workmen invaded the house; and hammer and plane sounded, and a general air of size and paint pervaded the atmosphere.
10150-8{_}931{_}One wing of the old house, the south, was entirely re-done; and then the great body of the workmen departed, leaving only materials for the doing of the old hall when Geoffrey Brent should have returned, for he had directed that the decoration was only to be done under his own eyes.
10150-8{_}932{_}He had brought with him accurate drawings of a hall in the house of his bride's father, for he wished to reproduce for her the place to which she had been accustomed.
10150-8{_}933{_}As the moulding had all to be re-done, some scaffolding poles and boards were brought in and laid on one side of the great hall, and also a great wooden tank or box for mixing the lime, which was laid in bags beside it.
10150-8{_}934{_}When the new mistress of Brent's Rock arrived the bells of the church rang out, and there was a general jubilation.
10150-8{_}935{_}She was a beautiful creature, full of the poetry and fire and passion of the South; and the few English words which she had learned were spoken in such a sweet and pretty broken way that she won the hearts of the people almost as much by the music of her voice as by the melting beauty of her dark eyes.
10150-8{_}936{_}Geoffrey Brent seemed more happy than he had ever before appeared; but there was a dark, anxious look on his face that was new to those who knew him of old, and he started at times as though at some noise that was unheard by others.
10150-8{_}937{_}And so months passed and the whisper grew that at last Brent's Rock was to have an heir.
10150-8{_}938{_}Geoffrey was very tender to his wife, and the new bond between them seemed to soften him.
10150-8{_}939{_}He took more interest in his tenants and their needs than he had ever done; and works of charity on his part as well as on his sweet young wife's were not lacking.
10150-8{_}940{_}He seemed to have set all his hopes on the child that was coming, and as he looked deeper into the future the dark shadow that had come over his face seemed to die gradually away.
10150-8{_}941{_}All the time Wykham Delandre nursed his revenge.
10150-8{_}942{_}Deep in his heart had grown up a purpose of vengeance which only waited an opportunity to crystallise and take a definite shape.
10150-8{_}943{_}His vague idea was somehow centred in the wife of Brent, for he knew that he could strike him best through those he loved, and the coming time seemed to hold in its womb the opportunity for which he longed.
10150-8{_}944{_}One night he sat alone in the living-room of his house.
10150-8{_}945{_}It had once been a handsome room in its way, but time and neglect had done their work and it was now little better than a ruin, without dignity or picturesqueness of any kind.
10150-8{_}946{_}He had been drinking heavily for some time and was more than half stupefied.
10150-8{_}947{_}He thought he heard a noise as of someone at the door and looked up.
10150-8{_}948{_}Then he called half savagely to come in; but there was no response.
10150-8{_}949{_}With a muttered blasphemy he renewed his potations.
10150-8{_}950{_}Presently he forgot all around him, sank into a daze, but suddenly awoke to see standing before him someone or something like a battered, ghostly edition of his sister.
10150-8{_}951{_}For a few moments there came upon him a sort of fear.
10150-8{_}952{_}The woman before him, with distorted features and burning eyes seemed hardly human, and the only thing that seemed a reality of his sister, as she had been, was her wealth of golden hair, and this was now streaked with grey.
10150-8{_}953{_}She eyed her brother with a long, cold stare; and he, too, as he looked and began to realise the actuality of her presence, found the hatred of her which he had had, once again surging up in his heart.
10150-8{_}954{_}All the brooding passion of the past year seemed to find a voice at once as he asked her:  'Why are you here?
10150-8{_}955{_}You're dead and buried.'
10150-8{_}956{_}'I am here, Wykham Delandre, for no love of you, but because I hate another even more than I do you!'
10150-8{_}957{_}A great passion blazed in her eyes.
10150-8{_}958{_}'Him?'
10150-8{_}959{_}he asked, in so fierce a whisper that even the woman was for an instant startled till she regained her calm.
10150-8{_}960{_}'Yes, him!'
10150-8{_}961{_}she answered.
10150-8{_}962{_}'But make no mistake, my revenge is my own; and I merely use you to help me to it.'
10150-8{_}963{_}Wykham asked suddenly:  'Did he marry you?'
10150-8{_}964{_}The woman's distorted face broadened out in a ghastly attempt at a smile.
10150-8{_}965{_}It was a hideous mockery, for the broken features and seamed scars took strange shapes and strange colours, and queer lines of white showed out as the straining muscles pressed on the old cicatrices.
10150-8{_}966{_}'So you would like to know!
10150-8{_}967{_}It would please your pride to feel that your sister was truly married!
10150-8{_}968{_}Well, you shall not know.
10150-8{_}969{_}That was my revenge on you, and I do not mean to change it by a hair's breadth.
10150-8{_}970{_}I have come here tonight simply to let you know that I am alive, so that if any violence be done me where I am going there may be a witness.'
10150-8{_}971{_}'Where are you going?'
10150-8{_}972{_}demanded her brother.
10150-8{_}973{_}'That is my affair!
10150-8{_}974{_}and I have not the least intention of letting you know!'
10150-8{_}975{_}Wykham stood up, but the drink was on him and he reeled and fell.
10150-8{_}976{_}As he lay on the floor he announced his intention of following his sister; and with an outburst of splenetic humour told her that he would follow her through the darkness by the light of her hair, and of her beauty.
10150-8{_}977{_}At this she turned on him, and said that there were others beside him that would rue her hair and her beauty too.
10150-8{_}978{_}'As he will,' she hissed; 'for the hair remains though the beauty be gone.
10150-8{_}979{_}When he withdrew the lynch-pin and sent us over the precipice into the torrent, he had little thought of my beauty.
10150-8{_}980{_}Perhaps his beauty would be scarred like mine were he whirled, as I was, among the rocks of the Visp, and frozen on the ice pack in the drift of the river.
10150-8{_}981{_}But let him beware!
10150-8{_}982{_}His time is coming!'
10150-8{_}983{_}and with a fierce gesture she flung open the door and passed out into the night.
10150-8{_}984{_}*       *       *       *       *  Later on that night, Mrs. Brent, who was but half-asleep, became suddenly awake and spoke to her husband:  'Geoffrey, was not that the click of a lock somewhere below our window?'
10150-8{_}985{_}But Geoffrey--though she thought that he, too, had started at the noise--seemed sound asleep, and breathed heavily.
10150-8{_}986{_}Again Mrs. Brent dozed; but this time awoke to the fact that her husband had arisen and was partially dressed.
10150-8{_}987{_}He was deadly pale, and when the light of the lamp which he had in his hand fell on his face, she was frightened at the look in his eyes.
10150-8{_}988{_}'What is it, Geoffrey?
10150-8{_}989{_}What dost thou?'
10150-8{_}990{_}she asked.
10150-8{_}991{_}'Hush!
10150-8{_}992{_}little one,' he answered, in a strange, hoarse voice.
10150-8{_}993{_}'Go to sleep.
10150-8{_}994{_}I am restless, and wish to finish some work I left undone.'
10150-8{_}995{_}'Bring it here, my husband,' she said; 'I am lonely and I fear when thou art away.'
10150-8{_}996{_}For reply he merely kissed her and went out, closing the door behind him.
10150-8{_}997{_}She lay awake for awhile, and then nature asserted itself, and she slept.
10150-8{_}998{_}Suddenly she started broad awake with the memory in her ears of a smothered cry from somewhere not far off.
10150-8{_}999{_}She jumped up and ran to the door and listened, but there was no sound.
10150-8{_}1000{_}She grew alarmed for her husband, and called out: 'Geoffrey!
10150-8{_}1001{_}Geoffrey!'
10150-8{_}1002{_}After a few moments the door of the great hall opened, and Geoffrey appeared at it, but without his lamp.
10150-8{_}1003{_}'Hush!'
10150-8{_}1004{_}he said, in a sort of whisper, and his voice was harsh and stern.
10150-8{_}1005{_}'Hush!
10150-8{_}1006{_}Get to bed!
10150-8{_}1007{_}I am working, and must not be disturbed.
10150-8{_}1008{_}Go to sleep, and do not wake the house!'
10150-8{_}1009{_}With a chill in her heart--for the harshness of her husband's voice was new to her--she crept back to bed and lay there trembling, too frightened to cry, and listened to every sound.
10150-8{_}1010{_}There was a long pause of silence, and then the sound of some iron implement striking muffled blows!
10150-8{_}1011{_}Then there came a clang of a heavy stone falling, followed by a muffled curse.
10150-8{_}1012{_}Then a dragging sound, and then more noise of stone on stone.
10150-8{_}1013{_}She lay all the while in an agony of fear, and her heart beat dreadfully.
10150-8{_}1014{_}She heard a curious sort of scraping sound; and then there was silence.
10150-8{_}1015{_}Presently the door opened gently, and Geoffrey appeared.
10150-8{_}1016{_}His wife pretended to be asleep; but through her eyelashes she saw him wash from his hands something white that looked like lime.
10150-8{_}1017{_}In the morning he made no allusion to the previous night, and she was afraid to ask any question.
10150-8{_}1018{_}From that day there seemed some shadow over Geoffrey Brent.
10150-8{_}1019{_}He neither ate nor slept as he had been accustomed, and his former habit of turning suddenly as though someone were speaking from behind him revived.
10150-8{_}1020{_}The old hall seemed to have some kind of fascination for him.
10150-8{_}1021{_}He used to go there many times in the day, but grew impatient if anyone, even his wife, entered it.
10150-8{_}1022{_}When the builder's foreman came to inquire about continuing his work Geoffrey was out driving; the man went into the hall, and when Geoffrey returned the servant told him of his arrival and where he was.
10150-8{_}1023{_}With a frightful oath he pushed the servant aside and hurried up to the old hall.
10150-8{_}1024{_}The workman met him almost at the door; and as Geoffrey burst into the room he ran against him.
10150-8{_}1025{_}The man apologised:  'Beg pardon, sir, but I was just going out to make some enquiries.
10150-8{_}1026{_}I directed twelve sacks of lime to be sent here, but I see there are only ten.'
10150-8{_}1027{_}'Damn the ten sacks and the twelve too!'
10150-8{_}1028{_}was the ungracious and incomprehensible rejoinder.
10150-8{_}1029{_}The workman looked surprised, and tried to turn the conversation.
10150-8{_}1030{_}'I see, sir, there is a little matter which our people must have done; but the governor will of course see it set right at his own cost.'
10150-8{_}1031{_}'What do you mean?'
10150-8{_}1032{_}'That 'ere 'arth-stone, sir: Some idiot must have put a scaffold pole on it and cracked it right down the middle, and it's thick enough you'd think to stand hanythink.'
10150-8{_}1033{_}Geoffrey was silent for quite a minute, and then said in a constrained voice and with much gentler manner:  'Tell your people that I am not going on with the work in the hall at present.
10150-8{_}1034{_}I want to leave it as it is for a while longer.'
10150-8{_}1035{_}'All right sir.
10150-8{_}1036{_}I'll send up a few of our chaps to take away these poles and lime bags and tidy the place up a bit.'
10150-8{_}1037{_}'No!
10150-8{_}1038{_}No!'
10150-8{_}1039{_}said Geoffrey, 'leave them where they are.
10150-8{_}1040{_}I shall send and tell you when you are to get on with the work.'
10150-8{_}1041{_}So the foreman went away, and his comment to his master was:  'I'd send in the bill, sir, for the work already done.
10150-8{_}1042{_}'Pears to me that money's a little shaky in that quarter.'
10150-8{_}1043{_}Once or twice Delandre tried to stop Brent on the road, and, at last, finding that he could not attain his object rode after the carriage, calling out:  'What has become of my sister, your wife?'
10150-8{_}1044{_}Geoffrey lashed his horses into a gallop, and the other, seeing from his white face and from his wife's collapse almost into a faint that his object was attained, rode away with a scowl and a laugh.
10150-8{_}1045{_}That night when Geoffrey went into the hall he passed over to the great fireplace, and all at once started back with a smothered cry.
10150-8{_}1046{_}Then with an effort he pulled himself together and went away, returning with a light.
10150-8{_}1047{_}He bent down over the broken hearth-stone to see if the moonlight falling through the storied window had in any way deceived him.
10150-8{_}1048{_}Then with a groan of anguish he sank to his knees.
10150-8{_}1049{_}There, sure enough, through the crack in the broken stone were protruding a multitude of threads of golden hair just tinged with grey!
10150-8{_}1050{_}He was disturbed by a noise at the door, and looking round, saw his wife standing in the doorway.
10150-8{_}1051{_}In the desperation of the moment he took action to prevent discovery, and lighting a match at the lamp, stooped down and burned away the hair that rose through the broken stone.
10150-8{_}1052{_}Then rising nonchalantly as he could, he pretended surprise at seeing his wife beside him.
10150-8{_}1053{_}For the next week he lived in an agony; for, whether by accident or design, he could not find himself alone in the hall for any length of time.
10150-8{_}1054{_}At each visit the hair had grown afresh through the crack, and he had to watch it carefully lest his terrible secret should be discovered.
10150-8{_}1055{_}He tried to find a receptacle for the body of the murdered woman outside the house, but someone always interrupted him; and once, when he was coming out of the private doorway, he was met by his wife, who began to question him about it, and manifested surprise that she should not have before noticed the key which he now reluctantly showed her.
10150-8{_}1056{_}Geoffrey dearly and passionately loved his wife, so that any possibility of her discovering his dread secrets, or even of doubting him, filled him with anguish; and after a couple of days had passed, he could not help coming to the conclusion that, at least, she suspected something.
10150-8{_}1057{_}That very evening she came into the hall after her drive and found him there sitting moodily by the deserted fireplace.
10150-8{_}1058{_}She spoke to him directly.
10150-8{_}1059{_}'Geoffrey, I have been spoken to by that fellow Delandre, and he says horrible things.
10150-8{_}1060{_}He tells to me that a week ago his sister returned to his house, the wreck and ruin of her former self, with only her golden hair as of old, and announced some fell intention.
10150-8{_}1061{_}He asked me where she is--and oh, Geoffrey, she is dead, she is dead!
10150-8{_}1062{_}So how can she have returned?
10150-8{_}1063{_}Oh!
10150-8{_}1064{_}I am in dread, and I know not where to turn!'
10150-8{_}1065{_}For answer, Geoffrey burst into a torrent of blasphemy which made her shudder.
10150-8{_}1066{_}He cursed Delandre and his sister and all their kind, and in especial he hurled curse after curse on her golden hair.
10150-8{_}1067{_}'Oh, hush!
10150-8{_}1068{_}hush!'
10150-8{_}1069{_}she said, and was then silent, for she feared her husband when she saw the evil effect of his humour.
10150-8{_}1070{_}Geoffrey in the torrent of his anger stood up and moved away from the hearth; but suddenly stopped as he saw a new look of terror in his wife's eyes.
10150-8{_}1071{_}He followed their glance, and then he too, shuddered--for there on the broken hearth-stone lay a golden streak as the point of the hair rose though the crack.
10150-8{_}1072{_}'Look, look!'
10150-8{_}1073{_}she shrieked.
10150-8{_}1074{_}'Is it some ghost of the dead!
10150-8{_}1075{_}Come away--come away!'
10150-8{_}1076{_}and seizing her husband by the wrist with the frenzy of madness, she pulled him from the room.
10150-8{_}1077{_}That night she was in a raging fever.
10150-8{_}1078{_}The doctor of the district attended her at once, and special aid was telegraphed for to London.
10150-8{_}1079{_}Geoffrey was in despair, and in his anguish at the danger of his young wife almost forgot his own crime and its consequences.
10150-8{_}1080{_}In the evening the doctor had to leave to attend to others; but he left Geoffrey in charge of his wife.
10150-8{_}1081{_}His last words were:  'Remember, you must humour her till I come in the morning, or till some other doctor has her case in hand.
10150-8{_}1082{_}What you have to dread is another attack of emotion.
10150-8{_}1083{_}See that she is kept warm.
10150-8{_}1084{_}Nothing more can be done.'
10150-8{_}1085{_}Late in the evening, when the rest of the household had retired, Geoffrey's wife got up from her bed and called to her husband.
10150-8{_}1086{_}'Come!'
10150-8{_}1087{_}she said.
10150-8{_}1088{_}'Come to the old hall!
10150-8{_}1089{_}I know where the gold comes from!
10150-8{_}1090{_}I want to see it grow!'
10150-8{_}1091{_}Geoffrey would fain have stopped her, but he feared for her life or reason on the one hand, and lest in a paroxysm she should shriek out her terrible suspicion, and seeing that it was useless to try to prevent her, wrapped a warm rug around her and went with her to the old hall.
10150-8{_}1092{_}When they entered, she turned and shut the door and locked it.
10150-8{_}1093{_}'We want no strangers amongst us three tonight!'
10150-8{_}1094{_}she whispered with a wan smile.
10150-8{_}1095{_}'We three!
10150-8{_}1096{_}nay we are but two,' said Geoffrey with a shudder; he feared to say more.
10150-8{_}1097{_}'Sit here,' said his wife as she put out the light.
10150-8{_}1098{_}'Sit here by the hearth and watch the gold growing.
10150-8{_}1099{_}The silver moonlight is jealous!
10150-8{_}1100{_}See, it steals along the floor towards the gold--our gold!'
10150-8{_}1101{_}Geoffrey looked with growing horror, and saw that during the hours that had passed the golden hair had protruded further through the broken hearth-stone.
10150-8{_}1102{_}He tried to hide it by placing his feet over the broken place; and his wife, drawing her chair beside him, leant over and laid her head on his shoulder.
10150-8{_}1103{_}'Now do not stir, dear,' she said; 'let us sit still and watch.
10150-8{_}1104{_}We shall find the secret of the growing gold!'
10150-8{_}1105{_}He passed his arm round her and sat silent; and as the moonlight stole along the floor she sank to sleep.
10150-8{_}1106{_}He feared to wake her; and so sat silent and miserable as the hours stole away.
10150-8{_}1107{_}Before his horror-struck eyes the golden-hair from the broken stone grew and grew; and as it increased, so his heart got colder and colder, till at last he had not power to stir, and sat with eyes full of terror watching his doom.
10150-8{_}1108{_}*       *       *       *       *  In the morning when the London doctor came, neither Geoffrey nor his wife could be found.
10150-8{_}1109{_}Search was made in all the rooms, but without avail.
10150-8{_}1110{_}As a last resource the great door of the old hall was broken open, and those who entered saw a grim and sorry sight.
10150-8{_}1111{_}There by the deserted hearth Geoffrey Brent and his young wife sat cold and white and dead.
10150-8{_}1112{_}Her face was peaceful, and her eyes were closed in sleep; but his face was a sight that made all who saw it shudder, for there was on it a look of unutterable horror.
10150-8{_}1113{_}The eyes were open and stared glassily at his feet, which were twined with tresses of golden hair, streaked with grey, which came through the broken hearth-stone.
10150-8{_}1114{_}The Gipsy Prophecy   'I really think,' said the Doctor, 'that, at any rate, one of us should go and try whether or not the thing is an imposture.'
10150-8{_}1115{_}'Good!'
10150-8{_}1116{_}said Considine.
10150-8{_}1117{_}'After dinner we will take our cigars and stroll over to the camp.'
10150-8{_}1118{_}Accordingly, when the dinner was over, and the _La Tour_ finished, Joshua Considine and his friend, Dr Burleigh, went over to the east side of the moor, where the gipsy encampment lay.
10150-8{_}1119{_}As they were leaving, Mary Considine, who had walked as far as the end of the garden where it opened into the laneway, called after her husband:  'Mind, Joshua, you are to give them a fair chance, but don't give them any clue to a fortune--and don't you get flirting with any of the gipsy maidens--and take care to keep Gerald out of harm.'
10150-8{_}1120{_}For answer Considine held up his hand, as if taking a stage oath, and whistled the air of the old song, 'The Gipsy Countess.'
10150-8{_}1121{_}Gerald joined in the strain, and then, breaking into merry laughter, the two men passed along the laneway to the common, turning now and then to wave their hands to Mary, who leaned over the gate, in the twilight, looking after them.
10150-8{_}1122{_}It was a lovely evening in the summer; the very air was full of rest and quiet happiness, as though an outward type of the peacefulness and joy which made a heaven of the home of the young married folk.
10150-8{_}1123{_}Considine's life had not been an eventful one.
10150-8{_}1124{_}The only disturbing element which he had ever known was in his wooing of Mary Winston, and the long-continued objection of her ambitious parents, who expected a brilliant match for their only daughter.
10150-8{_}1125{_}When Mr. and Mrs. Winston had discovered the attachment of the young barrister, they had tried to keep the young people apart by sending their daughter away for a long round of visits, having made her promise not to correspond with her lover during her absence.
10150-8{_}1126{_}Love, however, had stood the test.
10150-8{_}1127{_}Neither absence nor neglect seemed to cool the passion of the young man, and jealousy seemed a thing unknown to his sanguine nature; so, after a long period of waiting, the parents had given in, and the young folk were married.
10150-8{_}1128{_}They had been living in the cottage a few months, and were just beginning to feel at home.
10150-8{_}1129{_}Gerald Burleigh, Joshua's old college chum, and himself a sometime victim of Mary's beauty, had arrived a week before, to stay with them for as long a time as he could tear himself away from his work in London.
10150-8{_}1130{_}When her husband had quite disappeared Mary went into the house, and, sitting down at the piano, gave an hour to Mendelssohn.
10150-8{_}1131{_}It was but a short walk across the common, and before the cigars required renewing the two men had reached the gipsy camp.
10150-8{_}1132{_}The place was as picturesque as gipsy camps--when in villages and when business is good--usually are.
10150-8{_}1133{_}There were some few persons round the fire, investing their money in prophecy, and a large number of others, poorer or more parsimonious, who stayed just outside the bounds but near enough to see all that went on.
10150-8{_}1134{_}As the two gentlemen approached, the villagers, who knew Joshua, made way a little, and a pretty, keen-eyed gipsy girl tripped up and asked to tell their fortunes.
10150-8{_}1135{_}Joshua held out his hand, but the girl, without seeming to see it, stared at his face in a very odd manner.
10150-8{_}1136{_}Gerald nudged him:  'You must cross her hand with silver,' he said.
10150-8{_}1137{_}'It is one of the most important parts of the mystery.'
10150-8{_}1138{_}Joshua took from his pocket a half-crown and held it out to her, but, without looking at it, she answered:  'You have to cross the gipsy's hand with gold.'
10150-8{_}1139{_}Gerald laughed.
10150-8{_}1140{_}'You are at a premium as a subject,' he said.
10150-8{_}1141{_}Joshua was of the kind of man--the universal kind--who can tolerate being stared at by a pretty girl; so, with some little deliberation, he answered:  'All right; here you are, my pretty girl; but you must give me a real good fortune for it,' and he handed her a half sovereign, which she took, saying:  'It is not for me to give good fortune or bad, but only to read what the Stars have said.'
10150-8{_}1142{_}She took his right hand and turned it palm upward; but the instant her eyes met it she dropped it as though it had been red hot, and, with a startled look, glided swiftly away.
10150-8{_}1143{_}Lifting the curtain of the large tent, which occupied the centre of the camp, she disappeared within.
10150-8{_}1144{_}'Sold again!'
10150-8{_}1145{_}said the cynical Gerald.
10150-8{_}1146{_}Joshua stood a little amazed, and not altogether satisfied.
10150-8{_}1147{_}They both watched the large tent.
10150-8{_}1148{_}In a few moments there emerged from the opening not the young girl, but a stately looking woman of middle age and commanding presence.
10150-8{_}1149{_}The instant she appeared the whole camp seemed to stand still.
10150-8{_}1150{_}The clamour of tongues, the laughter and noise of the work were, for a second or two, arrested, and every man or woman who sat, or crouched, or lay, stood up and faced the imperial looking gipsy.
10150-8{_}1151{_}'The Queen, of course,' murmured Gerald.
10150-8{_}1152{_}'We are in luck tonight.'
10150-8{_}1153{_}The gipsy Queen threw a searching glance around the camp, and then, without hesitating an instant, came straight over and stood before Joshua.
10150-8{_}1154{_}'Hold out your hand,' she said in a commanding tone.
10150-8{_}1155{_}Again Gerald spoke, _sotto voce_: 'I have not been spoken to in that way since I was at school.'
10150-8{_}1156{_}'Your hand must be crossed with gold.'
10150-8{_}1157{_}'A hundred per cent.
10150-8{_}1158{_}at this game,' whispered Gerald, as Joshua laid another half sovereign on his upturned palm.
10150-8{_}1159{_}The gipsy looked at the hand with knitted brows; then suddenly looking up into his face, said:  'Have you a strong will--have you a true heart that can be brave for one you love?'
10150-8{_}1160{_}'I hope so; but I am afraid I have not vanity enough to say "yes".'
10150-8{_}1161{_}'Then I will answer for you; for I read resolution in your face--resolution desperate and determined if need be.
10150-8{_}1162{_}You have a wife you love?'

10150-8{_}1164{_}'Then leave her at once--never see her face again.

10150-8{_}1166{_}Go quick--go far, and never see her face again!'

10150-8{_}1235{_}The dim twilight had waked some very tender feelings in her breast, and her eyes were full of gentle tears.

10150-8{_}1253{_}After a little while Mary recovered from her swoon, but only to fall into strong hysterics, in which she laughed and wept and raved and cried, 'Keep him from me--from me, Joshua, my husband,' and many other words of entreaty and of fear.
10150-8{_}1254{_}Joshua Considine was in a state of mind bordering on agony, and when at last Mary became calm he knelt by her and kissed her feet and hands and hair and called her all the sweet names and said all the tender things his lips could frame.
10150-8{_}1255{_}All that night he sat by her bedside and held her hand.
10150-8{_}1256{_}Far through the night and up to the early morning she kept waking from sleep and crying out as if in fear, till she was comforted by the consciousness that her husband was watching beside her.
10150-8{_}1257{_}Breakfast was late the next morning, but during it Joshua received a telegram which required him to drive over to Withering, nearly twenty miles.
10150-8{_}1258{_}He was loth to go; but Mary would not hear of his remaining, and so before noon he drove off in his dog-cart alone.
10150-8{_}1259{_}When he was gone Mary retired to her room.
10150-8{_}1260{_}She did not appear at lunch, but when afternoon tea was served on the lawn under the great weeping willow, she came to join her guest.
10150-8{_}1261{_}She was looking quite recovered from her illness of the evening before.
10150-8{_}1262{_}After some casual remarks, she said to Gerald: 'Of course it was very silly about last night, but I could not help feeling frightened.
10150-8{_}1263{_}Indeed I would feel so still if I let myself think of it.
10150-8{_}1264{_}But, after all these people may only imagine things, and I have got a test that can hardly fail to show that the prediction is false--if indeed it be false,' she added sadly.
10150-8{_}1265{_}'What is your plan?'
10150-8{_}1266{_}asked Gerald.
10150-8{_}1267{_}'I shall go myself to the gipsy camp, and have my fortune told by the Queen.'
10150-8{_}1268{_}'Capital.
10150-8{_}1269{_}May I go with you?'
10150-8{_}1270{_}'Oh, no!
10150-8{_}1271{_}That would spoil it.
10150-8{_}1272{_}She might know you and guess at me, and suit her utterance accordingly.
10150-8{_}1273{_}I shall go alone this afternoon.'
10150-8{_}1274{_}When the afternoon was gone Mary Considine took her way to the gipsy encampment.
10150-8{_}1275{_}Gerald went with her as far as the near edge of the common, and returned alone.
10150-8{_}1276{_}Half-an-hour had hardly elapsed when Mary entered the drawing-room, where he lay on a sofa reading.
10150-8{_}1277{_}She was ghastly pale and was in a state of extreme excitement.
10150-8{_}1278{_}Hardly had she passed over the threshold when she collapsed and sank moaning on the carpet.
10150-8{_}1279{_}Gerald rushed to aid her, but by a great effort she controlled herself and motioned him to be silent.
10150-8{_}1280{_}He waited, and his ready attention to her wish seemed to be her best help, for, in a few minutes, she had somewhat recovered, and was able to tell him what had passed.
10150-8{_}1281{_}'When I got to the camp,' she said, 'there did not seem to be a soul about, I went into the centre and stood there.
10150-8{_}1282{_}Suddenly a tall woman stood beside me.
10150-8{_}1283{_}"Something told me I was wanted!"
10150-8{_}1284{_}she said.
10150-8{_}1285{_}I held out my hand and laid a piece of silver on it.
10150-8{_}1286{_}She took from her neck a small golden trinket and laid it there also; and then, seizing the two, threw them into the stream that ran by.
10150-8{_}1287{_}Then she took my hand in hers and spoke: "Naught but blood in this guilty place," and turned away.
10150-8{_}1288{_}I caught hold of her and asked her to tell me more.
10150-8{_}1289{_}After some hesitation, she said: "Alas!
10150-8{_}1290{_}alas!
10150-8{_}1291{_}I see you lying at your husband's feet, and his hands are red with blood."'
10150-8{_}1292{_}Gerald did not feel at all at ease, and tried to laugh it off.
10150-8{_}1293{_}'Surely,' he said, 'this woman has a craze about murder.'
10150-8{_}1294{_}'Do not laugh,' said Mary, 'I cannot bear it,' and then, as if with a sudden impulse, she left the room.
10150-8{_}1295{_}Not long after Joshua returned, bright and cheery, and as hungry as a hunter after his long drive.
10150-8{_}1296{_}His presence cheered his wife, who seemed much brighter, but she did not mention the episode of the visit to the gipsy camp, so Gerald did not mention it either.
10150-8{_}1297{_}As if by tacit consent the subject was not alluded to during the evening.
10150-8{_}1298{_}But there was a strange, settled look on Mary's face, which Gerald could not but observe.
10150-8{_}1299{_}In the morning Joshua came down to breakfast later than usual.
10150-8{_}1300{_}Mary had been up and about the house from an early hour; but as the time drew on she seemed to get a little nervous and now and again threw around an anxious look.
10150-8{_}1301{_}Gerald could not help noticing that none of those at breakfast could get on satisfactorily with their food.
10150-8{_}1302{_}It was not altogether that the chops were tough, but that the knives were all so blunt.
10150-8{_}1303{_}Being a guest, he, of course, made no sign; but presently saw Joshua draw his thumb across the edge of his knife in an unconscious sort of way.
10150-8{_}1304{_}At the action Mary turned pale and almost fainted.
10150-8{_}1305{_}After breakfast they all went out on the lawn.
10150-8{_}1306{_}Mary was making up a bouquet, and said to her husband, 'Get me a few of the tea-roses, dear.'
10150-8{_}1307{_}Joshua pulled down a cluster from the front of the house.
10150-8{_}1308{_}The stem bent, but was too tough to break.
10150-8{_}1309{_}He put his hand in his pocket to get his knife; but in vain.
10150-8{_}1310{_}'Lend me your knife, Gerald,' he said.
10150-8{_}1311{_}But Gerald had not got one, so he went into the breakfast room and took one from the table.
10150-8{_}1312{_}He came out feeling its edge and grumbling.
10150-8{_}1313{_}'What on earth has happened to all the knives--the edges seem all ground off?'
10150-8{_}1314{_}Mary turned away hurriedly and entered the house.
10150-8{_}1315{_}Joshua tried to sever the stalk with the blunt knife as country cooks sever the necks of fowl--as schoolboys cut twine.
10150-8{_}1316{_}With a little effort he finished the task.
10150-8{_}1317{_}The cluster of roses grew thick, so he determined to gather a great bunch.
10150-8{_}1318{_}He could not find a single sharp knife in the sideboard where the cutlery was kept, so he called Mary, and when she came, told her the state of things.
10150-8{_}1319{_}She looked so agitated and so miserable that he could not help knowing the truth, and, as if astounded and hurt, asked her:  'Do you mean to say that _you_ have done it?'
10150-8{_}1320{_}She broke in, 'Oh, Joshua, I was so afraid.'
10150-8{_}1321{_}He paused, and a set, white look came over his face.
10150-8{_}1322{_}'Mary!'
10150-8{_}1323{_}said he, 'is this all the trust you have in me?
10150-8{_}1324{_}I would not have believed it.'
10150-8{_}1325{_}'Oh, Joshua!
10150-8{_}1326{_}Joshua!'

10150-8{_}1328{_}Joshua thought a moment and then said: 'I see how it is.
10150-8{_}1329{_}We shall better end this or we shall all go mad.'
10150-8{_}1330{_}He ran into the drawing-room.
10150-8{_}1331{_}'Where are you going?'
10150-8{_}1332{_}almost screamed Mary.
10150-8{_}1333{_}Gerald saw what he meant--that he would not be tied to blunt instruments by the force of a superstition, and was not surprised when he saw him come out through the French window, bearing in his hand a large Ghourka knife, which usually lay on the centre table, and which his brother had sent him from Northern India.
10150-8{_}1334{_}It was one of those great hunting-knives which worked such havoc, at close quarters with the enemies of the loyal Ghourkas during the mutiny, of great weight but so evenly balanced in the hand as to seem light, and with an edge like a razor.
10150-8{_}1335{_}With one of these knives a Ghourka can cut a sheep in two.
10150-8{_}1336{_}When Mary saw him come out of the room with the weapon in his hand she screamed in an agony of fright, and the hysterics of last night were promptly renewed.
10150-8{_}1337{_}Joshua ran toward her, and, seeing her falling, threw down the knife and tried to catch her.
10150-8{_}1338{_}However, he was just a second too late, and the two men cried out in horror simultaneously as they saw her fall upon the naked blade.
10150-8{_}1339{_}When Gerald rushed over he found that in falling her left hand had struck the blade, which lay partly upwards on the grass.
10150-8{_}1340{_}Some of the small veins were cut through, and the blood gushed freely from the wound.
10150-8{_}1341{_}As he was tying it up he pointed out to Joshua that the wedding ring was severed by the steel.
10150-8{_}1342{_}They carried her fainting to the house.
10150-8{_}1343{_}When, after a while, she came out, with her arm in a sling, she was peaceful in her mind and happy.
10150-8{_}1344{_}She said to her husband:  'The gipsy was wonderfully near the truth; too near for the real thing ever to occur now, dear.'
10150-8{_}1345{_}Joshua bent over and kissed the wounded hand.
10150-8{_}1346{_}The Coming of Abel Behenna   The little Cornish port of Pencastle was bright in the early April, when the sun had seemingly come to stay after a long and bitter winter.
10150-8{_}1347{_}Boldly and blackly the rock stood out against a background of shaded blue, where the sky fading into mist met the far horizon.
10150-8{_}1348{_}The sea was of true Cornish hue--sapphire, save where it became deep emerald green in the fathomless depths under the cliffs, where the seal caves opened their grim jaws.
10150-8{_}1349{_}On the slopes the grass was parched and brown.
